    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer12535310820849780302">"It's finished. There isn't a stamp, or an error that I haven't collected. Not one.   <span id="freeText12535310820849780302" style="display:none">"It's finished. There isn't a stamp, or an error that I haven't collected. Not one. What shall I do now?" <br />"I think I'm beginning to understand," said Moomintroll slowly. "You aren't a collector anymore, you're only an owner, and that isn't nearly so much fun." <br /><br />My children and I believed we were only "owners" of the Moomins nowadays, not collectors of their adventures. However, by accident we discovered that one can collect the same stamp twice, and be a happy Hemul. No stamp is an identical twin. To put it in a less Moominish way: we all of a sudden discovered we wanted to reread our collection of Moomins. And what a strange experience it is to read aloud to three teenagers who suddenly understand all the character traits of the inhabitants of Moomin Valley. When we started comparing and contrasting with whom we identified most, I added some valuable memory stamps to my rich collection of "reading with my children". My son said he now knew exactly why I need to be alone sometimes. If you wander off alone, you will be all the happier when you return. <br /><br />As for the wizard - what a kind and wise old man he turned out to be. <br /><br />Knowing people makes them less scary. And just remember to offer them pancakes. That is the ultimate test.<br /><br />Loved it!</span>

<div id="review_773227482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773227482" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/773227482?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=magical-creatures">magical-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=translations">translations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773227482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12015687954982544041">I absolutely adore Tove Jansson's Moomintrolls and their exploits, and the 1970s German language translations by Vivica and Kurt Bandler were favourites of my childhood (and are still considered sweet and nostalgic gems to be reread over and over again, although my copies are falling apart and I now need to find replacements). And with this fact in mind, when the Children's Literature Group decided to read Elizabeth Portch's English language translation of the third Moomintroll book, of <u>Trollkar</u></span>
  <span id="freeText12015687954982544041" style="display:none">I absolutely adore Tove Jansson's Moomintrolls and their exploits, and the 1970s German language translations by Vivica and Kurt Bandler were favourites of my childhood (and are still considered sweet and nostalgic gems to be reread over and over again, although my copies are falling apart and I now need to find replacements). And with this fact in mind, when the Children's Literature Group decided to read Elizabeth Portch's English language translation of the third Moomintroll book, of <u>Trollkarlens Hatt</u> a couple of years ago (in 2010 to be exact), I joined with eager and yes even glad anticipation, although I did wonder why Ms. Portch had chosen the title of <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u>, as it kind of harkens back to Johann D. Wyss' classic <u>Swiss Family Robinson</u> (and I definitely failed to see and still have trouble understanding how and why a group of Scandinavian troll like creatures should somehow be related in any manner to a tale of a Swiss family marooned on a deserted island). But that all being said, and my happy reading anticipation notwithstanding, <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u> has in many if not most ways been a major and sad disappointment, both in 2010 and still remaining thus for my recent reread (which I engaged in both to finally post a real review and also because I did want to give Elizabeth Portch's translation a second chance, but my disappointment with <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u> persists and rather massively so I might add).<br /><br />Now I do still enjoy and appreciate the characters, the plot, the events, the ideas presented in <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u>, but indeed have had rather massive amounts of trouble getting even remotely into the flow of the presented English language narrative. And considering how much I personally have always and repeatedly enjoyed the 1970s German translations of precisely this same book (and others of the Moomintroll series), I do absolutely believe that it is mores than likely Elizabeth Porch's to and for me rather mediocre translation that has caused this rather annoying sense of disconnection and being on the outside looking in (and yes, at times even tedious boredom, something that I certainly NEVER once experienced with Vivica and Kurt Bandler's always engaging and adventuresome renditions of Jansson's original Swedish). And thus, while I still do more than love and adore the 1970s German translations of the Moomintroll series that had graced and sweetened my childhood, I can only and will only consider but two stars for <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u>, as the flow and rhythm of Elizabeth Portch's translated text (or rather the lack of the former, the lack of adequate narrative flow and rhythm) is and continues to be both annoying and disappointing enough to in no way be able to consider a higher ranking (and also making me ever more eager to reread the Bandlers' 1970s German language translations).</span>
  <a data-text-id="12015687954982544041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3186990014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3186990014" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3186990014?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=classic-children-s">classic-children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3186990014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14932310595692987216">Marketed as a standalone novel (although it is technically part 3 of a series), <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i> is one of those books written for children, but that endures as a classic for all ages. I'm not sure if it's the quirky characters, the wonderful illustrations or the imagination poured into the story that does it, but this book has been immensely popular for a <i>long</i> time. It also inspired much of the first season of the 1990's cartoon adaptation for television.<br/><br/>The book consists of several chap</span>
  <span id="freeText14932310595692987216" style="display:none">Marketed as a standalone novel (although it is technically part 3 of a series), <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i> is one of those books written for children, but that endures as a classic for all ages. I'm not sure if it's the quirky characters, the wonderful illustrations or the imagination poured into the story that does it, but this book has been immensely popular for a <i>long</i> time. It also inspired much of the first season of the 1990's cartoon adaptation for television.<br /><br />The book consists of several chapters containing the misadventures of Moomin, a child growing up with his friends in a fantasy world where magic and strange occurrences are a regular thing. As fun as the stories themselves are, the endearing characters and good moral lessons make this book much deeper than initial appearances would imply. One of the biggest themes is that the characters who would be expected the most to be villainous are not really so scary after all, and that doing good for others makes everyone happy. Sounds childish and like common sense ideas, but the book puts it all together in a very memorable way.<br /><br />Whether it's encountering a mysterious sorcerer who rides a black panther and hunts for rare gemstones or fearing a terrifying monster that freezes anything it touches, i&gt;Finn Family Moomintroll is full of surprises, and it's easy to see why it has been around as long as it has while still inspiring new media adaptations and gaining fans the world over. At first I had no real interest in reading this book, but I'm glad I gave it a chance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14932310595692987216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10898866985992207803">As a child, I loved The Moomins, and as an adult, I adore them, and I think my obsession with them has gone just one step further. I mean, I have Moomin candles, a tea caddy, plushes, a bag, various mugs and a beautiful Moomin poster, right above my bookcase.   <span id="freeText10898866985992207803" style="display:none">As a child, I loved The Moomins, and as an adult, I adore them, and I think my obsession with them has gone just one step further. I mean, I have Moomin candles, a tea caddy, plushes, a bag, various mugs and a beautiful Moomin poster, right above my bookcase. They shaped my childhood, and if one needs an excuse to visit Covent Garden in London, The Moomin shop is a good enough reason in my humble opinion.<br /><br />This book is beautifully presented, with a pull out map of Moominland in it, which just adds to the magic. The stories are gorgeously written, allowing one to feel they are on an adventure with Moomin and his dear friends. Reading this book, has made me want to watch The Moomins original TV series again. <br /><br />This was a delightful trip down memory lane, and I intend to read more from Tove Jannsson in the near future. <br /> </span>

  <span id="freeText13262601491893755637" style="display:none"><b>Growing up with the Moomintrolls could be every child's wish because Moominmamma loves all her family no matter what they do.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579611814i/28816340._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>The Hobgoblins magic hat had changed Moomintroll into a strange creature. Moomintroll felt behind him with a trembling paw.<br><br>'Your eyes are like soup-plates,' said Sniff. 'Moomintroll's are small and kind!'<br><br>'Yes, exactly,' Snufkin agreed.<br><br>'You are an impostor!' decided the Hemulen.<br><br>'Isn't there anyone who believes me?' Moomintroll pleaded. 'Look carefully at me, mother. You must know your own Moomintroll.'<br><br>Moominmamma looked carefully. She looked into his frightened eyes for a very long time, and then she said quietly: 'Yes, you are my Moomintroll.'<br><br>And at the same moment he began to change. His ears, eyes, and tail began to shrink, and his nose and tummy grew, until at last he was his old self again.<br><br>'It's all right now, my dear,' said Moominmamma. She packed it all with an umbrella, warm clothes, tummy-ache medicine, an egg-whisk, cushions, a mosquito-net, bathing-drawers and a table cloth in her bag. She bustled to and fro racking her brains for anything she had forgotten, and at last she said: 'Now it's ready! Oh, how lovely it will be to have a rest by the sea!'<br><br>Moominpappa packed his pipe and his fishing-rod. 'Well, are you all ready?' he asked, 'and are you sure you haven't forgotten anything? All right, let's start!'<br><br><i>...a little time later...</i><br>Moominmamma hunted in all her baskets for a bottle of raspberry juice.'Oh dear, how sad!' she burst out.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3009698350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16515680926652851725">(in Finnish/Swedish - "The Magician's Hat", first released in Swedish (1948), then in Finnish 10 years later. Some later books were translated faster.) I like how you don't really need to start from the beginning in this series. Some parts of the book are already familiar to me; there's no Little My in this book...<br/><br/>So: one day after the moonmintrolls have woken up from their winter hibernation, Moomintroll goes with his friends to look around a nearby mountain, where they find a strange top hat; </span>
  <span id="freeText16515680926652851725" style="display:none">(in Finnish/Swedish - "The Magician's Hat", first released in Swedish (1948), then in Finnish 10 years later. Some later books were translated faster.) I like how you don't really need to start from the beginning in this series. Some parts of the book are already familiar to me; there's no Little My in this book...<br /><br />So: one day after the moonmintrolls have woken up from their winter hibernation, Moomintroll goes with his friends to look around a nearby mountain, where they find a strange top hat; they later learn it can change things into other things, mostly fun, but not always (like when it changes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Moomintroll for a while, but luckily Moominmamma recognises him so the change back happens faster <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). A lot of fun and scary things happen after that, including an island trip, and a battle with a sea creature. And two small creatures bring something secret with them, as they seek shelter in the Moomin house....<br /><br />I've read about the winter hibernation the moomins have; it's nice to read about the details (starts in November when snow arrives, not-moomins can also do it). And the whistle codes between friends is also cute! The magician actually makes a brief appearance already in a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[winter dream, though the hat is not found until spring <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The visit to the island was interesting, and how they think about the gold is interesting: good garden decoration! And I love Moominmamma's attitude, care, and cooking skills (eggs, pancakes with jam, coffee, tasty bubble and squeak-like dish (pyttipanna <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyttipanna">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyttipanna</a>), sandwiches.... she actually makes pancakes in a bathtub for a great party). <br /><br />I love how although there are dangerous moments, sad moments, exciting moments, happy moments and pondering moments, everything is cleared and everyone is happy in the end; and the magician is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not a particularly aggressive and possessive in the end, but is perfectly happy to grant some wishes for everyone at the party <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which surprised me in a happy way. Although I knew some of the details from cartoons/comics in a sort of passive way, the reading of this story made everything so rich, with great atmosphere.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16515680926652851725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">probably almost everybody, unless they have identical taste to mine</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103529434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2063090218115832125">I feel sacrilegious in rating this book with just 2 stars. I almost “graded” it higher.<br/><br/>I apologize to everyone who loves this book. I’ve gotten over it now, but for years I was extremely perturbed when others I knew didn’t love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/895953.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Series___1_' title='A Wrinkle in Time (Time Series, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wrinkle in Time</a> and some of my other favorites.<br/><br/>I apologize to The Muskrat (who is a real hoot) and to Moominmamma (because she really is a great character) and some of the other characters too. I apologize to the author because there were glimmers and glimpses throughou</span>
  <span id="freeText2063090218115832125" style="display:none">I feel sacrilegious in rating this book with just 2 stars. I almost “graded” it higher.<br /><br />I apologize to everyone who loves this book. I’ve gotten over it now, but for years I was extremely perturbed when others I knew didn’t love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/895953.A_Wrinkle_in_Time__Time_Series___1_" title="A Wrinkle in Time (Time Series, #1) by Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wrinkle in Time</a> and some of my other favorites.<br /><br />I apologize to The Muskrat (who is a real hoot) and to Moominmamma (because she really is a great character) and some of the other characters too. I apologize to the author because there were glimmers and glimpses throughout the book of a book I’d have found great, including a few choice lines that I appreciated greatly.<br /><br />Thanks to all the members of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/188.Children_s_Books" rel="nofollow noopener">Children's Books group</a> who kept me motived to continue reading by explaining why they loved this book/series in this thread: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/343179-june-2010-finn-family-moomintroll-finland">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/3...</a>, and who also gave some specific information helpful to enjoying the story, including a link to a character list. And thanks to my old Goodreads friend Jenny (who unfortunately left Goodreads shortly after she’d joined – we used to incessantly discuss the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/86236.Into_the_Forest" title="Into the Forest by Jean Hegland" rel="nofollow noopener">Into the Forest</a> at a time when very, very few Goodreads members had shelved it and when only two of my real world friends had read it) who was (I think) from Finland and who raved about these books, which is why I read an owned copy.<br /><br />I had an excruciatingly difficult time getting into this story. I felt irritable while reading it. If not for the help I received from the Children's Books group members in understanding the book and its background, I doubt I'd have enjoyed it at all. This might be due, in part, to my mood at the time of reading it and my stage of life.<br /><br />It didn’t help that I needed a magnifying glass to read the letter to the reader and the map (yes, this book does have one of my beloved maps!) at the beginning of the book.<br /><br />There are hints of psychological sophistication and wry humor, and it seems to be the kind of tale I “should” enjoy.<br /><br />I hated the positive depiction of tobacco.<br /><br />I loved the mother sending the kids to the cave until they were in better moods and really enjoyed it when the house turned into/grew overgrown with foliage because of the magic hat.<br /><br />I eventually warmed to the characters, though I do wish I had first read the book where they were first introduced: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1003725.Comet_in_Moominland__Moomins_" title="Comet in Moominland (Moomins) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Comet in Moominland</a> because I might have enjoyed them from the beginning rather than being confused by them; in this book there is a lack of introduction to the world/characters. I also ended up enjoying some of the events that take place. However, I didn’t like the writing style, which I blame on the translation. (Never have I wished so fervently that I could read Swedish or Finnish.)<br /><br />This book has the same feel to me as Winnie-the-Pooh, other books I never read as a child but read one of them only after I was a Goodreads member. I liked that one better than this, even though the sense of humor in this is much more sophisticated and probably better able to be appreciated by adults as well as by children.<br /><br /> The illustrations were very cute, but I think I’d have enjoyed them more if I’d known something, anything, about the characters before I’d started reading.<br /><br />I will keep thinking and if I ever read the earlier book, I’ll try to reread this book too and see if I like it any better the second time around.<br /><br />And, pay no attention to me, but take a look at the ratings breakdown for this book. Obviously. I’m not a typical reader of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2063090218115832125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15855969636094829820">I loved the Moomins so much as a kid. I don't remember reading them, actually -- surprisingly, no sense of location or of my fingers on the pages comes back to me, though usually I'll remember where I read books and whether my edition was new or old, and the smell of the pages...   <span id="freeText15855969636094829820" style="display:none">I loved the Moomins so much as a kid. I don't remember reading them, actually -- surprisingly, no sense of location or of my fingers on the pages comes back to me, though usually I'll remember where I read books and whether my edition was new or old, and the smell of the pages... In any case, I do remember that I loved the Moomins, and it was lovely to curl up and reread now I'm older, and wiser, and really not feeling well.<br /><br />I do love the range of characters, all with different customs and such, that just happily get along. And I love everyone's consideration of everyone else's different needs. It's... accepting, and hopefully inspiring, without being the slightest bit preachy.</span>

<div id="review_100702984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100702984" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112377-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217926616p2/112377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100702984?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/112377-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112377-kim?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112377-kim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100702984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10836638533817504402">As part of a "read a new book, reread an old book challenge" and because it's the 65th anniversary of the Moomin series (there's even a Moominweek at tor.com!), I decided to reread as much as I could of the Moomin series. Which ended up being only one book, unfortunately: <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>. I read this series when I was perhaps 8 or 9 years old, and loved it; I think it would also be a great choice to read aloud to younger children. The illustrations are adorable, and the names of the char</span>
  <span id="freeText10836638533817504402" style="display:none">As part of a "read a new book, reread an old book challenge" and because it's the 65th anniversary of the Moomin series (there's even a Moominweek at tor.com!), I decided to reread as much as I could of the Moomin series. Which ended up being only one book, unfortunately: <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>. I read this series when I was perhaps 8 or 9 years old, and loved it; I think it would also be a great choice to read aloud to younger children. The illustrations are adorable, and the names of the characters fun to say---the Snork, Hattifatteners, Thingumy and Bob--and in <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>, each of the chapters tells of a self-standing episode, although they are linked by the device of the Hobgoblin's hat.<br /><br />If you've never read the Moomin books before, you may be wondering exactly what a Moomin is. They are round fuzzy creatures who look like white hippopotamuses and who live in Moominvalley, in a house that resembles a Finnish fireplace. Akin to the Moomins are the Snorks, who look just the same in the black and white illustrations, but who change color according to their moods. In fact, the little girl Snork, the Snork Maiden, has a crush on Moomintroll, the little boy Moomin. Moomins hibernate through the winter, and awaken in the spring. <br /><br />On the first spring day the Moomins awaken from their hibernation, and Moomintroll decides to go on an expedition to the mountains with his friends, Sniff and Snufkin. In their explorations, the three children stumble upon a fine top hat, which they bring home, though it ends up being too big for everyone to wear. Instead, the hat is put to use as a wastebasket, and Moomintroll throws away his eggshells in it. Shortly thereafter, five small clouds appear, and the children amuse themselves by floating around upon them. From this point, the story primarily involves transformations brought about by putting things into the hat, some of them fun and positive, like the clouds, some of them not. <br /><br />As you can probably tell, the Moomin books are very silly and imaginative, and it's really refreshing to read a book in which you never have to worry that things will work out in the end. There's not really a villain in <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>, though there are some characters who aren't pleasant: the eerie Hattifatteners, for instance, and the Groke, who freezes the ground wherever she walks. Yet even in the cheery and fanciful world of Moominvalley, there are hints of melancholy, which will become more pronounced in the later books of the series. The Groke, for instance, is very lonely and isolated by her condition; Moomintroll, while normally a cheerful child, doesn't understand Snufkin's need to wander off by himself. Though I never found him as cute as the Moomins---he always looked to me like a scarecrow, only wearing a smock---Snufkin was probably the character I identified with the most as a child, specifically because he was balanced the joy of spending time with friends and the peace of being alone. But I really loved most of the characters, even the grumpy Muskrat and the fussbudget Hemulen. If you love absurdist fantasy and have a sense of whimsy, I'm willing to bet you will, too!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10836638533817504402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_59191159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59191159" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/343944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242156693p2/343944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59191159?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/343944-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380003501" href="/book/show/1036906.Finn_Family_Moomintroll">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=my-happy-childhood">my-happy-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=read-aloud">read-aloud</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59191159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15151697276863533931">Sometimes things do work out as they ought to: my son is well on the road to loving the Moomintroll books just as much as I do. We breezed through this second book in the series really fast -- T was able, without much effort, to persuade Mama to read a chapter aloud pretty much any time of day, as long as he wasn't supposed to be in school.<br/><br/>This charming tale of one Spring and Summer in the lives of the Moomin family picks up where its predecessor left off. Every member of the Moomin household fr</span>
  <span id="freeText15151697276863533931" style="display:none">Sometimes things do work out as they ought to: my son is well on the road to loving the Moomintroll books just as much as I do. We breezed through this second book in the series really fast -- T was able, without much effort, to persuade Mama to read a chapter aloud pretty much any time of day, as long as he wasn't supposed to be in school.<br /><br />This charming tale of one Spring and Summer in the lives of the Moomin family picks up where its predecessor left off. Every member of the Moomin household from the previous book is still there in this one, a circumstance that never repeats itself. It opens with Moomintroll and his friends Snufkin and Sniff waking up from their long Winter sleep on the first day of Spring, a day when everything is fresh and anything seems possible. Atop a local mountain which they impulsively climb, they discover a hat which they soon learn has some surprising magical properties.<br /><br />The different transformations wrought by the hat over the next few months give the book an episodic feel, and to an extent, I missed the sense of urgency and narrative momentum which the impending arrival of the comet provides in the first book. However, a more meandering storyline suits Jansson's whimsical style just fine, and ironically, considering that in the first book Moomintroll and his friends went off alone into the wilds and encountered many great dangers, this one speaks more, in its quiet way, of growing up and making one's own choices. After Moomintroll's parents decide that the hat is dangerous, they try to get rid of it by throwing it into the river. Snufkin and Moomintroll sneak out late at night to retrieve it. <i>"You know", said Moomintroll seriously, "it's the first time we have done anything that we can't tell mother and father about."</i> And indeed, even though their motivation for wanting the hat back is the fun that the hat has given them, they have done the right thing and discovered that parents, as much as one loves them, are not infallible. Throwing the hat in the river where it was wreaking havoc on the ecosystem, turning water into raspberry juice and fish into canaries was a pretty terrible idea! But the greater lesson for Moomintroll is that the joys of being out at night, of being Snufkin's most trusted friend, and eventually, after they have hidden the hat, of seeing a lovely sunrise on the beach -- these are a far greater magic than anything produced by the hat. <br /><br />There is a sadder lesson at the end of the book, when as Autumn begins to arrive, Snufkin decides to leave his friends and wander South: sometimes we have to say goodbye to the people we love the most. I had been surprised at the beginning of the book that Snufkin had spent the previous Winter hibernating with the Moomins. That seemed out of character for him, and I suppose it was the last time he did it. Ultimately though, the book is joyful, and the hobgoblin's magic turns Moomintroll's sense of loss into one of expectancy. And everyone has a lot of fun in the meantime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15151697276863533931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6805283887516251772">The troll toy craze first arrived in the UK around 1962. I was 7 and I begged for one of these little dolls. I must have really wanted it as I never asked my parents for anything. Mum wasn't too impressed. Tried hard to dissuade me but perhaps the novelty of her daughter's passionate appeal won her over. How I treasured that toy. <br/><br/>I did not encounter Moomintroll and friends however until a year or two later and did not really associate the two in my mind. My toy was a troll... These were Moomins.</span>
  <span id="freeText6805283887516251772" style="display:none">The troll toy craze first arrived in the UK around 1962. I was 7 and I begged for one of these little dolls. I must have really wanted it as I never asked my parents for anything. Mum wasn't too impressed. Tried hard to dissuade me but perhaps the novelty of her daughter's passionate appeal won her over. How I treasured that toy. <br /><br />I did not encounter Moomintroll and friends however until a year or two later and did not really associate the two in my mind. My toy was a troll... These were Moomins. Nevertheless it was again love at first sight. The cover of the puffin book was delightful and as for the stories.... So quirky and a celebration of free spirit. Everything was OK. Moominmamna did not, it seemed, bat an eyelid at anything... All visitors were welcome no matter how eccentric and Moomintroll could go off n adventures whenever he fancied. Ah that's the life.... <br /><br />Sadly troll has come to mean a very different kind of animal now. Something much closer to it's Nordic origins.. A person bent on destroying the pleasure of others.. Where's a big billy goat gruff when you need one? </span>

<div id="review_3036769179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3036769179" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3036769179?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780374323288" href="/book/show/1036905.Finn_Family_Moomintroll">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers Who Enjoy Quirky Fantasy Fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=finnish-children">finnish-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-translations">childrens-translations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3036769179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1884842647600111466">Delightfully idiosyncratic, wholly original, and immensely engaging, this charming fantasy from Finnish author Tove Jansson is a classic of world children's literature, and it is not difficult to see why. The tale of an eclectic family of beings who live together in Moominvalley - distracted Moominpappa, always writing his memoirs; kind but fair-minded Moominmamma, with her all-essential handbag; sweet Moomintroll himself, so anxious for everyone to get along; the somewhat aloof Snufkin, a music</span>
  <span id="freeText1884842647600111466" style="display:none">Delightfully idiosyncratic, wholly original, and immensely engaging, this charming fantasy from Finnish author Tove Jansson is a classic of world children's literature, and it is not difficult to see why. The tale of an eclectic family of beings who live together in Moominvalley - distracted Moominpappa, always writing his memoirs; kind but fair-minded Moominmamma, with her all-essential handbag; sweet Moomintroll himself, so anxious for everyone to get along; the somewhat aloof Snufkin, a musician with wanderlust, if ever there was one - it somehow manages to be both unhurried and exciting, involving the reader in its characters' adventures - finding the Hobgoblin's hat, and discovering its unusual qualities, sailing to the Lonely Island, and encountering the Hattifatteners - as well as their inner emotional lives.<br /><br />I loved so many things about <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u>, from Jansson's hilarious little footnotes, to her adorable illustrations, that it's difficult to single out what it is that makes the story so appealing. In the end, after much discussion over in the children's books group to which I belong - where this was our June selection, for <i>The International Book Club</i> - I have settled on three essential qualities to Jansson's creation, that make it truly outstanding. To wit: the respect that the Moomins show to one another, and through them, that Jansson shows for her readers; the sly humor to be found in both text and image; and the tolerance - the celebration, even - of diversity and difference.<br /><br />These are highly individual characters all, with distinct interests and personalities, but there is always the sense that they are welcome. I was particularly struck by the way in which the Moomintroll household seems to continually be expanding to include newcomers. Bob and Thingummy, for instance, arrive toward the end of the book, and Moominmamma's first thought, when she discovers that their language is difficult to understand - that they are, in a sense, "foreigners" - is not, <i>"what are they doing here?"</i> but <i>"how will I know what to make them for their special birthday feast, if we can't communicate?"</i> Although the incorporation of these two is the only family expansion that occurs within the book's narrative, the text hints that other members were likewise adopted, in the past.<br /><br />This generosity of spirit is reflected, not only in the welcoming of new (and highly unusual) family members, but in the way that the established Moomins interact with each other. Every one has their flaws, but Jansson invites us to accept and forgive them, recognizing that, despite these failings, they are each an important part of the whole. The Hemulen, for instance, may be a bit of an obsessive-compulsive collector, more interested in the process of amassing objects than in really studying them, but that in no way means he isn't a feeling creature - someone to be treated with consideration. This is made clear in the scene, early on, when Moomintroll and the Snork Maiden discover him in the forest, deeply upset. Concerned, but also respectful, they avoid pressing him for details, but make it clear that they are there to listen.<br /><br />Of course, all this analysis might lead one to suppose that <u>Finn Family Moomintroll</u> was a very serious book, but nothing could be further from the truth! Jansson has a subtle but very appealing sense of humor, that emerges in sly little asides - as when she writes of the Hemulen: <i>"(he) continued to look worried because he thought he oughtn't to look happy after such a big sorrow"</i> - and humorous incidents, like the one in which the Muskrat barrels past the beach-bound Moomins. The adventures themselves - whether it be Moomintroll and friends riding on the little egg-shell clouds, or the Moomin family each discovering something washed up on the shore of the Hattifatteners' island, after the big storm - are absolutely magical, and young readers wills wish that similar things might happen to them.<br /><br />In short: this is that rarest of books which manages to succeed, both as entertainment and art, and I cannot recommend it highly enough! I have read bits and pieces of Tove Jansson's work, over the years - enough to know I liked it - but this is my first experience sitting down and reading one of her books straight through. All I can say is: where's the next?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1884842647600111466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I really, really liked this. It's like an odd cross between Wind in the Willows and Dr. Seuss. There are shallow characters, kind characters, vain characters, selfless characters, and characters with questionable morals all wrapped up in this funny little family who will accept anyone who seems to need a family. There's never any real sense of alarm, even when the Groke shows up, because everyone can be reasoned with or, at the very least least, bought. And where one person finds their limits, another steps in to help. It's adorable. I love it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14254042237972503834">The third in the series but the first to be translated into English. I think I prefer its original Swedish title: 'The Magician's Hat'. In this story, Moomintroll, Sniff and Snufkin discover a 'Hobgoblin's' hat which has the power to change anything placed within it. Although this is the plot device that binds all events together it's not for this that you really read the book but for the delightful characters, both new and old, that Jansson lovingly plays with. Why it has taken me so long to re</span>
  <span id="freeText14254042237972503834" style="display:none">The third in the series but the first to be translated into English. I think I prefer its original Swedish title: 'The Magician's Hat'. In this story, Moomintroll, Sniff and Snufkin discover a 'Hobgoblin's' hat which has the power to change anything placed within it. Although this is the plot device that binds all events together it's not for this that you really read the book but for the delightful characters, both new and old, that Jansson lovingly plays with. Why it has taken me so long to read these books is an question that shall remain forever unanswered. The fact that they are now in my life...well, that's pleasure enough for me. </span>

<div id="review_1591614912" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591614912?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah O&#39;Carroll" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah O&#39;Carroll" href="/user/show/19951545-deborah-o-carroll">Deborah O&#39;Carroll</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19951545-deborah-o-carroll?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19951545-deborah-o-carroll?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>,

<div id="review_3011270258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011270258" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478144-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450473p2/1478144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011270258?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/1478144-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011270258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16411008407327647180">This is actually a reread for me. However, since I romped through all the Moomin books when I was about ten or twelve, I don't think it really counts as such. That said, I was astonished by how much I remembered from well over a half-century ago. (My wife suggests I may have read it to my daughter when <i>she</i> was small, but I don't recall doing so -- shame on me for this failure of parenting! -- and, even if I did, that would still have been, ahem, a respectable number of years ago.)<br/><br/>Moomintroll, Sn</span>
  <span id="freeText16411008407327647180" style="display:none">This is actually a reread for me. However, since I romped through all the Moomin books when I was about ten or twelve, I don't think it really counts as such. That said, I was astonished by how much I remembered from well over a half-century ago. (My wife suggests I may have read it to my daughter when <i>she</i> was small, but I don't recall doing so -- shame on me for this failure of parenting! -- and, even if I did, that would still have been, ahem, a respectable number of years ago.)<br /><br />Moomintroll, Snufkin and Sniff find a stovepipe hat on a mountaintop and bring it home. What they don't realize is that it belongs to the Hobgoblin, which means that anything put inside it, from a set of false teeth to Moomintroll himself, changes into something completely different -- and unpredictably so: you have no way of knowing what the result of the transition will be.<br /><br />This is the pretext for a set of loosely linked stories relating the adventures through the spring, summer and fall of a single year of the Moomin family and their pals. There's a wonderfully refreshing pointlessness to the tales, endless inventiveness, and humor that sparkles to the extent that I started to get funny looks while reading <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i> in the doctor's waiting room while my wife was undergoing her checkup somewhere in the building's depths. (One old lady squinted across to see what I was giggling about, then gave me a complicit grin. Clearly another Moomin devotee.)<br /><br />We watched the completely bloody awful animated movie <i>Moomins and Midsummer Madness</i> (2008) a few months ago, and would advise others to avoid it. (I thought it might give my wife a hint as to why I'm such a fan of the books. Boy, did <i>that</i> backfire.) I understand <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i> (2014), which I've just learned about while checking the title of its predecessor, is better and, although jokes about low hurdles are inevitable, I'm keen to give it a try.<br /><br />I don't read Finnish but, to judge by Tove Jansson's illustrations, Elizabeth Portch's translation succeeds excellently in capturing the capricious anarchy of the original.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16411008407327647180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nTKa4+XJOvzWwtq3f77xp5i5/oxc4MU5J+SwLPY6/fvIIF4qbrZL7IwbfDva/lJtC6ub1QfYO8ccZzz2QKKGew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q3eaqKrr2Y7JnnvmiafFsDW3h+rh17Tg4If5RMcjY4z+ZV5hIZSonpNH3Wos52Z6pqXis7rvSh7bBHWecbsYDA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">About Tove Jansson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1419249529p3/45230.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">Tove Jansson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,423
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11555666531639498452"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText11555666531639498452" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11555666531639498452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
